2:43

The method is very simple. Imagine that you have a very long Excel sheet.
3:34

3:42
In English language, there are around 10,000 words in total. So, it is a very big Excel sheet in which all the words are written one by one.

4:02
If there is a cat, it is 3. If there is a dog, it is 4. Similarly, when I write a word, let's say, apple, ball, cat, the computer understands it as 1, 2, 3.
4:13
So, whenever you write 3, 2, 1 here, it means that for the computer, it will be cat, ball, apple.
4:20
So, this is a look-up table type for LLMs. Now, this process may seem very lengthy to you.
4:26

4:32
Well, for us humans, yes, it is tedious. But for computer systems, it is not that tedious.
4:38
So, all LLMs use a look-up table in a way. They use the number corresponding to any word.
4:44

4:55

6:22

6:35
You can think of these connections as a flip switch. Like a human neuron, one neuron does not do a lot of different things.
6:42
One neuron is sitting. Its job is to identify the yellow color from any scenery that is coming out of its eyes.
6:49
So, it will sit idle all the time. It will not do anything. As soon as it sees a yellow color coming out of your eyes, it will get triggered immediately.
6:58
See, I saw a yellow color. So, in the same way, all the neurons in the LLM models, which are different branches of the neural network, they are all for a specific task.
7:09
They are activated only for that task. Now, when we provide text to these models in a very large volume, provide content, it divides that content into different small pieces.
7:21
And it starts to find out the pattern. What is going to come after a particular word.
7:27
Now, it is not that when the training starts, all these switches know what to do.
7:33
They generate a loop in a way in which they guess the next word coming from any text.
7:39
And after that, the entire training data is seen whether the guess was accurate or not. If the guess was accurate, then that node is considered correct.
7:47
If it was not correct, then it is considered wrong. After that, another node is generated. So, this process is done by the computers themselves.
7:55
They do it simultaneously. And then, they develop a model which generates the next word after a particular word with a little accuracy.
8:10
So, overall, the final result model is based on the training data and whatever word it has seen before, on that basis, the next word does the work of guessing.
8:22
And this guess is based on a lot of data. That is why it is around accuracy. So, for example, if I say a line, then some of you will be able to guess the next word of that line.

8:52
Technically, you have guessed it. But you only had the context. So, LLM models also generate accuracy in the same way.

Because they have all the data of the world written in the world, all the text, all the content, all the data from the images.
9:09

So whatever system will be like Perplexity, it will send the query to its vector database, which is made of its own data.

What were the related chunks sent by the query embedding?

1:30
So, why is the removal tool required? Let's say that there was a disgruntled employee in your company, who created a random page on your website, which is harmful, which should not be on your website, and Google indexes it.
1:43
Now, you go to your website and remove that page, you try your best, but still, that content is being shown in Google search.
1:51
Such scenarios can happen many times, and Google search does not provide any live support, where you delete a page from your website,
2:00
and Google immediately removes it from the index. So, in such scenarios, the removal tool helps us to remove any particular page from the Google index immediately.
2:09
How immediately? If you enter any particular URL in the removal tool, it is removed from Google search within 2-3 hours.
2:18
You will put a request from your Google search console, and it will be removed within 2-3 hours.
2:26
Okay, it will not be in the index. But here, it is important to keep in mind that this is a temporary removal. Now, what does temporary removal mean? If you remove any URL from the Google search index by using the removal tool, then it is only removed for 6 months, not forever.
2:39
So, does this mean that the page can come back after 6 months? Yes, it can come back, if you have not deleted it from your website.
2:47
So, if you want to completely remove a page from Google search, then you will have to delete that page from your website first.
2:56
When someone visits that URL, there should be a 404 status code. For example, if I come here and want to visit a URL, google.com
3:06
slash abracadabra. No one will say anything. Here, the page is 404. Okay. So, now this page is showing 404.
3:15
Similarly, if you want to remove a URL through the removal tool, let's say, the URL is abc.com, myceoisbad.
3:26
Someone has created a mischievous page like this. If you want to remove it, when someone visits this URL, then this URL should be 404.
3:33
Okay. In this way, a 404 status code should appear on this page. Once this 404 status code appears, after this, you will go to Google Search Console and remove this URL.
3:44
How will you remove it? Click on the New Request button. Here, we will type abc.com slash whatever URL it is.
3:52
Let's copy it completely and enter it here. After this, you can see two options here. Remove this URL only.
4:00
Remove all URLs with this prefix. So, this is an absolute URL on its own. Right. abc.com slash myceoisbad.

5:18

5:29
